  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_00d60d29-04cb-435b-a615-c38461729ae5'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText15671032129926125392" style="display:none">I must admit, Iâm not a big fan of books that people deem to be âmisery memoirsâ (I do not like that term). You know the kind: a parent abused their child/an outside person abused a child/drink addictions/drug addictions/etc. However, there are a few memoirs like that Iâve read. I absolutely loved âUglyâ by Constance Briscoe. It was so honest, so raw and despite being a tough read, I did like it. So when I was emailed about Katie Piperâs memoir I was intrigued. Iâd read her story in one of the weekly magazines â Take A Break or Chat or Thatâs Life or Pick Me Up or something, I canât remember. It vaguely rang a bell with me, however and I was interested to learn more about what had happened to Katie.<br /><br />Beautiful is a hard book to read. Katieâs spirit immediately leaps out of the pages as the book starts with her recounting her love of everything as a child. How she liked dressing up but how she also liked helping her dad with DIY projects so when you go to the part where Katie meets the man whoâs going to ruin her life it is hard to continue. It baffles me â in fact, I donât think baffles is a strong enough word â that there are human beings on this planet who do such bad things like that. How somebody can be so sick as to tell someone else to throw acid in somebodyâs face. Itâs unfathomable. Itâs heartbreaking to read how Katie was trying to make her mark in the TV presenting world and all of a sudden her face is ruined and sheâs struggling with staying alive.<br /><br />Itâs the kind of book you have to read to really believe. I know there are monsters everywhere in the world â people who murder, who abuse, who harm, who throw acid â but to read such a harrowing account of it, from the victimâs point of view is just amazing but not in that kind of way. What really makes this book amazing, though, is Katieâs eventual determination to not let the men ruin her life. Anybody who had their face ruined the way Katie did â and not just her face, but her life, her trust in people, her trust in leaving her house or the hospital â would be within their rights to curl up in a ball and wait to die. To never leave the house again. But not Katie Piper. Sure, her situation gets her down and it takes her time to go out in the world again, but she eventually realised she couldnât let it ruin her life forever and the way sheâs turned her life around is something special. Her life may not be what it once was, but sheâs just got on with it and made the best of what life she has now.<br /><br />Katie Piper is an inspiration. I felt humbled reading the book because I complain about the smallest things and yet look at what sheâs gone through. Look at what sheâs fought against and come back from. I think Iâm a pretty strong person, but I donât know if I could come back from something like that. Beautiful is an inspiring read and Katie is a heck of a person. As I said, I only vaguely knew her story when I heard about her book but to read Beautiful is so much more than reading a small article. This is Katieâs story, how it all happened from start to finish (well, not finish, to how her life is now) and itâs a mightily impressive read. Katie Piper can hold her head up high, which might sound twee but itâs true. She won. Those people who tried to destroy her life failed because look at her. Sure, itâs not the life she imagined for herself, but itâs a damn sight better than it could have been and she hasnât half made lemonade from the lemons she was given. A truly inspiring read.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer193915907791501134">Katie Piper's memoir of her journey through trauma to triumph is one of the most moving books I have ever read. She is absolutely raw on the page, exposing the darkest and lightest parts of her experience in equal measure and inviting the reader to view her very soul. It must have taken such courage to share herself so completely with the world.<br/><br/>But I suppose that's the thing that constantly strikes you about Katie as you read through these pages, her courage. She is tougher and stronger than I t</span>
  <span id="freeText193915907791501134" style="display:none">Katie Piper's memoir of her journey through trauma to triumph is one of the most moving books I have ever read. She is absolutely raw on the page, exposing the darkest and lightest parts of her experience in equal measure and inviting the reader to view her very soul. It must have taken such courage to share herself so completely with the world.<br /><br />But I suppose that's the thing that constantly strikes you about Katie as you read through these pages, her courage. She is tougher and stronger than I think she even acknowledges and an example to all of us of the gratitude and bravery we should display in our own lives.<br /><br />There were certainly parts of this book that were difficult to read, including some scenes of sexual violence. As a woman, I was horrified by what she had been through, by what had been done to her and by the daily psychological challenges she has to face. My admiration for her grew with each page I read as did my disgust for the heinous monsters who attacked her. 16 years seems too short a sentence for such violent and disturbing crimes.<br /><br />Katie's determination to not let them beat her and to build a new and rewarding life for herself was amazing. She has endured countless surgeries and hospital visits and rebuilt herself both physically and mentally. And she is still an absolutely gorgeous young woman! I encourage you to look up the Katie Piper Foundation and learn more about the work she and her team do for burns victims. <br /><br />Katie, the world is lucky to have you and your beautiful smile in it. Thank you for sharing your story with us.</span>

How could I look like that?â<br /><br />âThe police had agreed to put Danny in one of those glass boxes; he couldnât get me. heâd be locked inside.â <br /><br />âIn the last twelve months, Iâd seen humanity at its worst, and its best, too. Had it made me a better person, deep down, underneath the scars?â<br /><br />ââ¦the judgeâs sentencing remarks, which had also been quoted in all the news stories: â[The victim] had a face of pure beauty. You, Danny Lynch and Stefan Sylvestre, represent the face of pure evil.â<br /><br />ââThe facts of this case are chilling and shocking. You planned and then executed an act of pure, calculated and deliberate evil. You decided to wreck the victimâs life by thrusting a full container of sulphuric acid straight into her face from point blank range.ââ<br /><br />ââOne of the hardest things about being disfigured is getting over how other people view or react to you.ââ<br /><br />My Review:<br /><br />	My Amazon records indicate that I purchased this book. I honestly donât remember. I only know that I am glad I found the book and read it. It is an amazing story of courage and how one young woman fought back to live. I think the book blurb and the quotes I use speak for themselves in recommending this book. Beautiful details how Katie set her life goals and worked hard towards attaining them, only to have them ripped from her. She fought through adversity and won. I recommend this book and even though I do not rate books, I give it 5 out of 5 stars.<br /></span>

<div id="review_457277543" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/457277543" />
    <a title="Jeffrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8838650-jeffrey"><img alt="Jeffrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368452603p2/8838650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/457277543?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey" href="/user/show/8838650-jeffrey">Jeffrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8838650-jeffrey?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer457277543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12179804271703977543">Fantastic, heart-breaking, inspiring! I could NOT put it down.<br/><br/>I was vaguely familiar with Katie Piper's odyssey but after reading a couple of articles on the internet I bought the book. I pronounce this autobiography as the best of its particular type I have ever read.<br/><br/>Miss Piper's story is so fantastic that it reads more like a fictional account than something that really happened to a real person. For someone who absolutely relied on her beautiful appearance to make a living in British media, w</span>
  <span id="freeText12179804271703977543" style="display:none">Fantastic, heart-breaking, inspiring! I could NOT put it down.<br /><br />I was vaguely familiar with Katie Piper's odyssey but after reading a couple of articles on the internet I bought the book. I pronounce this autobiography as the best of its particular type I have ever read.<br /><br />Miss Piper's story is so fantastic that it reads more like a fictional account than something that really happened to a real person. For someone who absolutely relied on her beautiful appearance to make a living in British media, what happened to Katie was almost a fate worse than death. A jilted boyfriend brutally raped her, then had an accomplice throw industrial-strength sulphuric acid in her face! Her plastic surgeon said he had never seen a more horribly chemically burned face than Katie's. Her left eye had been blinded, she lost most of her left ear, most of her nose, her eyelids, and her esophagus was permanently damaged by swallowing acid to the point that she could not eat solid foods for a lengthy period of time.<br /><br />Her story starts with her happy, optimistic childhood, her efforts to become a media celebrity in the U.K., the nightmarish destruction and disfigurement of her face, initially her wish to just die, her dozens of surgical treatments, her stark terror of men and morbid agoraphobia, her dedicated struggle to regain her appearance, and finally acceptance of her rebuilt face and her gratitude for all who helped her.<br /><br />For someone who is not a professional writer, Katie's writing has impact, urgency, and conveys her innermost feelings with gripping emotion. The graphic photos of her burned face are simply horrifying. Katie's dramatic surgical results (and I do mean DRAMATIC) are the result of her plastic surgeon's decision to do a radical and never-before-tried full-face skin graft using a combination of actual donor skin and a recently developed artificial skin for the first time together. She also received several experimental therapy treatments at a burn clinic spa in France. Her discipline in undergoing a rigorous and painful rehabilitation regimen is a testimony to her striving to get her life back to something that would resemble "normal."<br /><br />She now has her own full-time foundation where she raises funds for others who have been disfigured by burns, injuries, and birth defects. The "after" photos in the book show how miraculous her transformation has been. Even more recent pics in the British media show even more improvement. Her "before" and "after" images have to be seen to be believed!<br /><br />Prepare to be mesmerized, thrilled, and emotionally caught up in Katie's heroic story of courage and hope. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12179804271703977543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer862752536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16904602449089941368">A book club choice (the best of a bad bunch), I've been embarrassed to have this on my bedside table in hospital and asked my partner to bring me a "proper" book to restore my literary street cred with the medical team. <i>Beautiful</i> has such a naff cover and font, it's one step down from beach lit... kiosk lit? Airport lit? It looks and reads like a 300 page edition of <i>Grazia</i> or another cheap women's magazine containing some woman's tragic but true story. The good thing about reading this coming ou</span>
  <span id="freeText16904602449089941368" style="display:none">A book club choice (the best of a bad bunch), I've been embarrassed to have this on my bedside table in hospital and asked my partner to bring me a "proper" book to restore my literary street cred with the medical team. <i>Beautiful</i> has such a naff cover and font, it's one step down from beach lit... kiosk lit? Airport lit? It looks and reads like a 300 page edition of <i>Grazia</i> or another cheap women's magazine containing some woman's tragic but true story. The good thing about reading this coming out of surgery myself is that it kept my own health issues, operation and treatments in perspective. Reading Piper's horrific story makes me feel lucky about my own impending journey back to health. <br /><br />There is no denying that Katie Piper has been through a terrible ordeal and made the best out of an awful situation by starting her foundation and looking to help others. Good for her! I hope that other burn victims get to benefit from the treatments she is hoping to implement in the UK with the help of her foundation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16904602449089941368" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4498351930176842466">This book was wonderful. I cried at many parts over the kindness and courage that people showed during such harrowing times. An evil man tried to ruin a beautiful girl's dreams that fateful day but he picked the wrong girl. Katie has a strength and beauty and kindness that even acid cannot touch.   <span id="freeText4498351930176842466" style="display:none">This book was wonderful. I cried at many parts over the kindness and courage that people showed during such harrowing times. An evil man tried to ruin a beautiful girl's dreams that fateful day but he picked the wrong girl. Katie has a strength and beauty and kindness that even acid cannot touch. Her incredible journey from wannabe to victim to hero is something we need to hear to remind us that we must appreciate our lives now, we must never give up, things do get better and above all: love wins. Katie isn't just a beautiful girl who lost her face and then through strength and courage claimed it back, she is beauty, inside and out. She is beauty personified.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13368677587140183833">Inspirational!<br/><br/>Not usually a fan of this genre of book (as Iâve stated in many other reviews here) but, in spite of this, I found this book to be quite a satisfying and very inspirational read.<br/><br/>All credit to Piper that she was able to reclaim her life and selfhood after becoming victim to a devastating acid attack all cruelly arranged and set up by her evil mess of a boyfriend who had raped her just hours before.<br/><br/>Itâs when you read books like these that you realise how simply rotten some humans can</span>
  <span id="freeText13368677587140183833" style="display:none">Inspirational!<br /><br />Not usually a fan of this genre of book (as Iâve stated in many other reviews here) but, in spite of this, I found this book to be quite a satisfying and very inspirational read.<br /><br />All credit to Piper that she was able to reclaim her life and selfhood after becoming victim to a devastating acid attack all cruelly arranged and set up by her evil mess of a boyfriend who had raped her just hours before.<br /><br />Itâs when you read books like these that you realise how simply rotten some humans can be and thus Piperâs book offers a sense of triumph of the human spirit demonstrating that many people are indeed good people and good souls â fortunately she had these types of people in abundance around her in her years of recovery after the attack.<br /><br />Spiritually and because it deals with difficult (to say the least!) subject matter, the book is quite a hard-going read. Piper doesnât seem to hold back on her honesty (and nor should she!) and, as a result, taking in some of the subject matter is difficult to digest without feeling angry at perpetrators of such crime and hatred. After both of these criminals received life sentences, Piper worked hard at restoring ânormalityâ into her life and her narration ends just after the point where she established the âKatie Piper Foundationâ to help better quality of life and availability of restorative medical treatment to other victims.<br /><br />As narrated, the tone of the book is very eloquent and Piper does give a great deal of insight into her own situation. The same eloquence, emotional intelligence and fighting spirit are popular qualities demonstrated by her during the plethora of television work she undertakes to publicise disfigurement issues and to raise public awareness about them.<br /><br />In short, one cannot fail to be inspired by such a read and such messages from âa real personâ who knows that beauty is so much more than skin deep. One cannot help but wish Katie Piper well for being a true and utter inspiration and a real woman of absolute courage too. <br /><br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1243608838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8388823730349936524">I have watched both of Katie's documentaries, the second of which 'Katie's Beautiful Friends' really touched me. I read this book in one sitting and I still keep thinking about it. Katie fully admits that before the attack she was into her looks and keeping herself slim. When she describes the attack and her subsequent recovery, it is quite harrowing. She had actually swallowed some of the acid when it was thrown at her and this left her with lots of problems where she found it hard to eat and s</span>
  <span id="freeText8388823730349936524" style="display:none">I have watched both of Katie's documentaries, the second of which 'Katie's Beautiful Friends' really touched me. I read this book in one sitting and I still keep thinking about it. Katie fully admits that before the attack she was into her looks and keeping herself slim. When she describes the attack and her subsequent recovery, it is quite harrowing. She had actually swallowed some of the acid when it was thrown at her and this left her with lots of problems where she found it hard to eat and she lost a lot of weight to the point she had to have a feeding tube inserted into her stomach for 8 months. She has endured many operations and has even been told that the strain of the operations on her liver and kidney's will effect her life expectancy. It never seemed that she was saying 'poor me'. Her Surgeon sounds absolutely brilliant and you can feel her love and respect for him throughout the book.<br />One interesting part for me was that in the documentaries, she has talked about dating again and whether anyone will find her attractive but then in the book, she does mention a boyfriend she had after the attack. I never knew this and she is honest about why she kept him out of the media and I can understand her reasons for why the relationship didn't work. He did sound like a lovely young man though...I hope that she does manage to find love in the future as she states quite often that she would like to be married with children.<br />I can't recommend this book highly enough. Well done Katie, you are truly beautiful, inside and out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8388823730349936524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

In this day and age I didn't think much could still shock me but her story truly has; I thought the attack in the hotel room and the days before the acid attack were even more shocking than the acid attack itself. She is inspiring and strong and a role model for any young woman; I really admire her. The world would be a better place if people idolized people like Katie instead of talentless celebs like Jordan etc<br />I hope Katie's attackers never get released from jail, they are pure evil.<br />Good luck Katie!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4231382251947054948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_922749846" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/922749846" />
    <a title="Lucy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15083337-lucy"><img alt="Lucy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486674659p2/15083337.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/922749846?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy" href="/user/show/15083337-lucy">Lucy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer922749846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17208438709011496815">I think this book for me has touched a part of me, I didn't know I had. I was a bit sceptical at first as I wasn't sure if this book would be too traumatic to read. <br/><br/>But it was so honest and beautiful even though it was dark and difficult to read. I found it particularly difficult to read, especially when Katie meets the man that is about to change her world, the only world she knows. But Katie is one of those people who just jumps out at you, she has so much energy and is very forward, she's the</span>
  <span id="freeText17208438709011496815" style="display:none">I think this book for me has touched a part of me, I didn't know I had. I was a bit sceptical at first as I wasn't sure if this book would be too traumatic to read. <br /><br />But it was so honest and beautiful even though it was dark and difficult to read. I found it particularly difficult to read, especially when Katie meets the man that is about to change her world, the only world she knows. But Katie is one of those people who just jumps out at you, she has so much energy and is very forward, she's the kind of person you'd meet at a party and just be in awe of her, she is a glow stick in a party of darkness. This memoir really captures that even from days gone by, when she was a child, she loved to learn how to do things, spending time with her Dad, helping him with projects, dressing up, being innocent. <br /><br />Katie's energy, confidence and vibrant personality was exactly what she needed to get noticed in the world of TV presenting, and she had been working hard at making her mark in her chosen career. For a while within these pages, it felt like disappeared after the harrowing acid attack which could have cost her her life. <br /><br />To Katie it must have felt like this world she had worked so hard for world felt like it had changed forever but with the personality she had it could never truly disappear. Her determination and the support from the health care professionals involved in her care (which Katie constantly praises) helped Katie to become this strong, beautiful woman once more. <br /><br />It's really hard to read how there are such monsters in this world though I already know this, but to read it and having had the person it happened to relieve these memories, thoughts and feelings for me to read again must have been incredibly testing at times. The man that did this is a pure monster but one that walks in the same skin as me and that is absolutely bone chillingly terrifying, to think that someone you know or knew could become this monster and enact a form of life changing punishment are just pure evil. To read it from a victim's point of view, it is incredibly touching and by the end of the book, you really feel that you know Katie on a personal level, I am in awe of her. You cannot take my word for it, you have to read it yourself. <br /><br />The determination Katie has is absolutely amazing and she completely deserves the recognition she has in this book, from all the professionals that worked with her, with her TV presenting career and more. She truly is an inspiration to others whether they have also been victim of acid attacks or have their own share of trauma. <br /><br />It hasn't been an easy ride for this woman but man, she deserves all the happiness in the world, the hard work has definitely been put in and from what I've read on her other books, she's getting pretty close to being happy with what she has in her life at the moment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17208438709011496815" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2013774304" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12719669812695718199">I must admit that I have never been a fan of Katie Piper because it seems she's only every programme everywhere I look and I would then have to turn off the TV when she inevitably appeared. However, I had heard great things about her book so decided to give it a go; I wholeheartedly admit I was far too quick to judge and I was completely wrong. Katie is such a likeable, wonderful person, who has triumphed over such adversity and has gone on to achieve great success. <br/><br/>I particularly liked how ther</span>
  <span id="freeText12719669812695718199" style="display:none">I must admit that I have never been a fan of Katie Piper because it seems she's only every programme everywhere I look and I would then have to turn off the TV when she inevitably appeared. However, I had heard great things about her book so decided to give it a go; I wholeheartedly admit I was far too quick to judge and I was completely wrong. Katie is such a likeable, wonderful person, who has triumphed over such adversity and has gone on to achieve great success. <br /><br />I particularly liked how there was minimal focus on Katie;s early years, as there can be in some biographies, as it's clear that people read this book as they want to know about the acid attack and how she dealt with it. For some reason it didn't quite hit five stars for me (nothing to do with the writing, as I really enjoyed the writing style here) but I feel there was something missing; maybe I wanted a little more detail in how she coped with everyday life, or how she set up her charity... I'm not exactly sure what I was looking for but I felt there could have been more. That being said, Katie has gone on to write at least one other biography, so I imagine she has gone on to explore in more depth there. I will definitely be reading any follow-ups!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12719669812695718199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Read this book if you feel like your life is a mess.You will soon realise is isn't, and be pleased to know you CAN pull yourself through anything. Just DON'T give up.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('643SqRBZjChjaAgamwmKsIqnIkj0A+cFPhBL8HghWYmVOP+wE35uAe7cKQGc3GA4NxKqXOmfO0jie1MorLyyqg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_17674582'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17674582-everything-to-live-for?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Everything to Live For: The Inspirational Story of Turia Pitt<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/7014788.Turia_Pitt?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Turia Pitt<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.23 avg rating &mdash; 985 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2013\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer34470378246731058\">Everything to Live For is the story of one young woman\'s survival against extraordinary odds, a testament to the human spirit.\n\nIn September 2011, Turia Pitt, a beautiful 23-year-old mining engineer working her dream job in the far north of Western A<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText34470378246731058\" style=\"display:none\">Everything to Live For is the story of one young woman\'s survival against extraordinary odds, a testament to the human spirit.\n\nIn September 2011, Turia Pitt, a beautiful 23-year-old mining engineer working her dream job in the far north of Western Australia, entered an ultra-marathon race that would change her life forever. Trapped by a fire in a gorge in the remote Kimberly region, Turia and five other competitors had nowhere to run. Turia escaped with catastrophic burns to 65 per cent of her body.\nWith too little unburned skin left for skin grafts, Turia was put in an induced coma in the Burns Unit at Sydney\'s Concord Hospital while her body fought life-threatening infections and her surgeons imported skin from California. She lost the fingers on her right hand and her fingers on her left are partially fused together. She needed a new nose. There have been numerous operation, yet there are many more to come.\nWhile the story of Turia\'s survival involves many people - other race competitors, her rescuers, medical professionals - at its core is the strong will of Turia herself as she continues the long rehabilitation process with the loving support of her partner, Michael Hoskins, and that of their families in their New South Wales south coast hometown of Ulladulla, where the local community has rallied, raising funds to help with huge medical bills.\n\nEverything to Live For is also a love story. Michael, Turia\'s handsome teenage crush who became the love of her life, now cares for her as they plan a new life together; he is there to encourage Turia in her determination to move forward in an outwardly different body.\nThe real tragedy of this story is that it should never have happened - because the race should never have happened. The findings against the organisers of the event, Racing the Planet, in a far-reaching parliamentary inquiry by the Western Australian Government in 2012, were damning.\n\nDespite facing a future with multiple challenges, Turia is optimistic. She is driving again and studying for her Master\'s degree. She is walking in marathons and would one day like to run again. Above all, she wants her story to make a difference: her mission is to make skin a more prominent organ in the repertoire of donated organs.\n\nIt is a miracle Turia lived when she was expected to die. But Turia was not ready to die - she had too much to live for.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"34470378246731058\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n He was an easy target for bullies and suffered terribly at their hands.\n\nIn a moment of inspiration, he decided to reinvent himself with his first style makeover and a larger-than-life personality to go with it.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4644729.Katie_Piper">About Katie Piper</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4644729.Katie_Piper"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1451320739p3/4644729.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2749783492918027070">Kate Elizabeth "Katie" Piper (born 12 October 1983) is a philanthropist, television presenter and former model from Andover, Hampshire in England, UK. Piper had hoped to have a full-time career in the media, but in March 2008 sulphuric acid was thrown in her face. The attack, which blinded Piper in one eye, was arranged by Piper's ex-boyfriend, Daniel Lynch, and carried out by an accomplice, Stefa</span>
  <span id="freeText2749783492918027070" style="display:none">Kate Elizabeth "Katie" Piper (born 12 October 1983) is a philanthropist, television presenter and former model from Andover, Hampshire in England, UK. Piper had hoped to have a full-time career in the media, but in March 2008 sulphuric acid was thrown in her face. The attack, which blinded Piper in one eye, was arranged by Piper's ex-boyfriend, Daniel Lynch, and carried out by an accomplice, Stefan Sylvestre. Lynch and Sylvestre were arrested and are serving life sentences in prison for their crimes.[1]<br />The attack took place in north London and Piper was treated in Chelsea and Westminster Hospital, where the surgeons removed all the skin from her face before rebuilding it with a skin substitute and then a skin graft. The procedure was the first of its kind to be completed in a single operation.[2][3]<br />In 2009, Piper chose to give up her anonymity in order to increase awareness about burn victims. The Channel 4 documentary Katie: My Beautiful Face was first aired on 29 October 2009 as part of the Cutting Edge series; it has subsequently been repeated on several occasions, made available for online on-demand access, and sold internationally.<br />More recently, Piper has appeared in a follow-up series for Channel 4, released a best-selling autobiography, and had a regular column in weekly magazine Reveal; however, she primarily works for her charitable organisation the Katie Piper Foundation.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2749783492918027070" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
